VIDEO 444

Source Type      : hashtag
Source Value     : stress
Video URL        : https://www.tiktok.com/@dramalinabakri/video/7083809941991017733

--- TEXT CONTENT ---
Caption:
How to manage stress? #TikTokUnpacks##tress ##indfulness @@TikTok @@TikTok UK

Transcript:
For stress awareness day, let's unpack stress management for TikTok and Packs. We all experience stress from time to time. Stress may be triggered by multiple factors including our surroundings, our bodies, our own ideas and perceptions of the world around us. We are normally physically equipped to deal with and react to stress. Stress hormones including noradrenaline, adrenaline and cortisol are released when we're stressed. We score the fight or flight response. Stress may be beneficial since it keeps us attentive, motivated and concentrated. However, problems emerge when we experience severe or continuous stress or when negative sensations outnumber our ability to cope. Continuous nervous system stimulation eliciting a stress response can cause the body to deteriorate. So how do you manage stress? First of all, maintain a healthy social support network. You don't have to cope with stress alone. Talk to your friends and families. Remove toxic people from your life. Secondly, look after your wellbeing. Give yourself a break. Look after yourself physically and engage in regular physical exercise. Working out on a daily basis is one of the most effective ways to calm your body and mind. Also, get enough sleep each night. Next, eat healthy balanced diet. Eating a well-balanced meal on a daily basis can help you feel better in general. It may also aid with mood regulation. Number four, take control of yourself. Be kind to yourself and accept that there are uncertainties in your life. Avoid dwelling things you can't control and take action over the things you can control. Focus on the present and what matters and don't seek perfection. Number five, prioritize your time and plan your timeline. It is important to set achievable goals. Don't push yourself too hard. Number six, give yourself a reward. Plan your holidays or do something that you love so that you have something to look forward to. And finally, please see your GP or mental health specialist if you're not coping. Remember, you're not alone.

--- TEXT CONTENT ---
Caption:
Could you be stressed without realizing it? #TikTokUnpacks #Stress #mindfulness

Transcript:
Could you be stressed without realizing it? This month, we're unpacking stress for TikTok Unpacks. Stress is what we feel when we're under pressure. It's a normal feeling that we all go through from time to time. Some people even find a small amount of stress to be helpful or motivating. But when we have too much pressure for too long, that's when we're in danger of having a severe stress reaction. And if left unmanaged, this can have consequences for your health in the long term. The signs of stress can be physical, emotional and behavioral. You might experience frequent headaches, muscle tension, aches and pains, even a racing heart or blurred vision. It's also common to feel constantly tired and exhausted. Emotionally, you may feel angry, irritable, impatient, full of dread, overwhelmed and frustrated. Feeling like this can have an impact on the way you see yourself, the world and others. What is considered stressful can vary from person to person, but it's important to remember that even things you may think are positive could be a source of stress. So here are some ways you can identify and beat stress. First, try keeping a stress diary to identify where, what and who may be making you stressed. Note what you feel, think and do when you're feeling stressed. Do you notice any patterns and are the behaviors you do in response to stress helping or making it worse? Challenge your thoughts. What advice would you give to your friend if they came to you with a stressful thought? Seeing your problems from the outside may give you a more useful perspective. And finally, prioritize your self-care. It's easy to let things pile up when you're feeling stressed. Remember it's okay to say no and take some time for yourself.

Caption:
Relaxing feels impossible for some people. Be honestâ€”does this sound like you? ðŸ§ #psychologyfacts #neuroscience #mentalhealth #brainfacts #stressrelief

Transcript:
Some people can't relax, even in peaceful moments. It's not because they don't want to, but because their brain doesn't know how. When your brain is constantly in alert mode, it starts to rewire itself. It learns to always search for danger. Even when nothing's wrong, your nervous system keeps scanning, waiting, preparing. Over time, your body forgets what safety even feels like. That's why lying in bed or sitting in silence can feel uncomfortable instead of peaceful. And here's the hidden part most people don't realize. The brain starts treating calmness itself as a threat. So the moment you finally slow down, the mind creates noise, restlessness, racing thoughts, even tension in your chest. It's almost like the body believes something must be wrong if it's not under stress. That's why so many people keep themselves busy, scrolling, working, distracting, not because they enjoy it, but because stillness feels unsafe. But the good news is the brain can learn again. Small signals of safety, like slow breathing, grounding your body or practicing short pauses, can slowly teach your nervous system that rest is safe. So if you've ever felt unable to relax, it's not laziness, it's biology. Save this if you need a reminder.

When someone dies by suicide, they don't end their pain, they transfer it. My late partner transferred hers to me, not intentionally, not to hurt me, but because pain doesn't just disappear, it has to land somewhere, and it landed right in the center of my life. And for a long time, I carried it like it was mine, the guilt, the questions, the sleepless nights, replaying every word, every moment. I thought if I could understand why, maybe the ache would make sense, or did, because they die of an illness of the mind. And over time, I realized something. The pain that she left wasn't meant to destroy me, it was really meant to be transformed through me. And so now, I live differently. I choose meaning over misery. I find purpose in the pain, in the chaos of what shouldn't have happened but did. I use the ache to help others, to listen deeper, to love harder. Her pain became my teacher, and it showed me how to grieve with more love than pain, and how to live for both us, not by carrying her suffering, but by turning it into something that heals, because grief doesn't have to end in darkness. I think sometimes, it's where the light begins, and that's my work now. Working with clients around the globe, teaching them to how to grieve with more love than pain. Keep going.
